### Round 1 | planner | planner_initial

- diagnosis: The task is to assess the likely AIE mechanism for a very large neutral boron-containing polyaryl molecule. From the prepared structure context, the current top1 is neutral aromatic and the top2 runner-up is ICT. TICT also remains a credible portfolio alternative because the scaffold has many aryl-aryl torsions and 14 rotatable bonds. ESIPT is presently weak because the molecule lacks a conventional proton-transfer motif, and unknown is retained only as residual uncertainty. The top1 is only a working hypothesis because current evidence is limited to structural proxies: donor-acceptor partition proxy is low, aromatic content is extremely high, and the scaffold is rotor-rich, but no direct excited-state observable has yet been gathered. Shared prepared structure context is available and ready, which supports a bounded first-round microscopic baseline calculation on the selected conformer. Macro can screen one deterministic structural evidence family such as donor-acceptor layout, rotor topology, or neutral-aromatic structural cues, but it cannot make a global mechanism decision. Microscopic can perform exactly one low-cost baseline S0/S1 action on the shared prepared structure, which may provide indirect evidence about excitation character, but it cannot in the first round run conformer sensitivity, torsion scans, or a multi-step discriminative workflow. Because both ICT and TICT remain credible and unscreened, the first round should gather both macro and microscopic evidence to reduce portfolio coverage debt rather than prematurely entering pairwise contraction.

- action: macro_and_microscopic

- confidence: 0.42

- task_instruction: Run one bounded macro screen for donor-acceptor layout and one bounded microscopic baseline S0/S1 action on the shared prepared structure to gather indirect evidence that can screen ICT and TICT against a neutral-aromatic working hypothesis.

- task_completion: Task completed successfully within current macro capability.

- task_understanding: The task is to assess macro-level structural evidence relevant to the current working hypothesis 'neutral aromatic' by reusing the shared prepared structure context and summarizing low-cost structural indicators within the current macro capability limits.

- reasoning_summary: The molecule is predominantly a neutral multi-aryl scaffold with weak donor-acceptor partitioning, consistent with the neutral aromatic hypothesis. However, the presence of boron acceptor centers and multiple torsional motifs leaves ICT and TICT as credible alternatives. To support or weaken the neutral aromatic hypothesis, structural evidence on aromatic core dominance, ring-system rigidity, and neutral-aromatic structural cues is needed. The shared prepared structure context is available and can be leveraged for deterministic topology and geometry-proxy analysis without resorting to fallback SMILES-only methods.
Capability limit note: Only deterministic low-cost single-molecule macro analysis is available. Aggregate-state modeling, packing simulation, and global mechanism adjudication are unsupported. The shared prepared structure context is used to avoid fallback to SMILES-only analysis.

The macro scan recorded aromatic_atom_count=72, hetero_atom_count=2, branch_point_count=34, rotatable_bond_count=14, planarity_proxy=0.987043, compactness_proxy=0.964276, and conformer_dispersion_proxy=1.0.
